    <dl>
           <dt>la 1</dt>
           <dd><em>la</em> the 3rd semivowel (corresponding to the vowels <em>&#x1e37;</em>, <em>&#x1e39;</em>, and having the sound of the English <em>l</em>) <font color="#FF0000" font size=-2><a name="p891-3"></a>[Page 891, Column 3]</font> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; a technical term for all the tenses and moods of a finite verb or for the terminations of those tenses and moods (also applied to some forms with <em>k&#x1e5b;t</em> affixes construed like a finite verb <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#P&#x0101;&#x1e47;">P&#x0101;&#x1e47;.</a> 2-3, 69 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#iii,">iii,.</a> 2, 124, and when accompanied by certain indicatory letters denoting each tense separately, <em>la&#x1e6d;</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>la&#x1e45;</em> </dd>

           <dd>&#x2022; (in gram.) dropping, elision (generally as distinguished from the terms <em>lup</em>, <em>&#x015b;lu</em>, <em>luk</em>, which are only applicable to affixes </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; when <em>lopa</em> of an affix takes place, a blank is substituted, which exerts the same influence on the base as the affix itself, but when either <em>luk</em> or <em>lup</em> or <em>&#x015b;lu</em> of an affix is enjoined, then the affix is not only dropped but it is also inoperative on the base </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; thus in the Ist pl. of <em>kati</em>, where <em>jas</em> is said to be elided by <em>luk</em>, the change of the final of the base to Gu&#x1e47;a does not take place, i.e. both the affix and its effect on the base are abolished </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; moreover, <em>lopa</em> refers only to the last letter of an affix, whereas by <em>luk</em> &amp;c. the dropping of the whole affix is implied) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Nir">Nir.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Pr&#x0101;t">Pr&#x0101;t.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#P&#x0101;&#x1e47;">P&#x0101;&#x1e47;.</a> &amp;c </dd>

           <dt>&#x226b; loka </dt>
           <dd><em>lok&#x00e1;</em> m. (connected with <em>roka</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in the oldest texts <em>loka</em> is generally preceded by <em>u</em>, which accord. to the <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Padap">Padap.</a> = the particle 3. <em>u</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; but <em>u</em> may be a prefixed vowel and <em>ulok&#x00e1;</em>, a collateral dialectic form of <em>loka</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; accord. to others <em>u-loka</em> is abridged from <em>uru-</em> or <em>ava-loka</em>), free or open space, room, place, scope, free motion <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Br">Br.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x0100;&#x015a;v&#x015a;r">&#x0100;&#x015a;v&#x015a;r.</a> (acc. with &#x221a;<em>k&#x1e5b;</em> or &#x221a;<em>d&#x0101;</em> or <em>anu-</em> &#x221a;<em>n&#x012b;</em>, to make room grant freedom' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>loke</em> with gen. 'instead of') </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; intermediate space <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Kau&#x015b;">Kau&#x015b;.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; a tract, region, district, country, province <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the wide space or world (either 'the universe' or, any division of it', esp. 'the sky or heaven' ; 3 Lokas are commonly enumerated, viz. heaven, earth, and the atmosphere or lower regions ; sometimes only the first two ; but a fuller classification gives 7 worlds, viz. Bh&#x016b;-l&#x1e6d;loka, the earth ; Bhuvar-l&#x1e6d;loka' the space between the earth and sun inhabited by Munis, Siddhas &amp;c. ; Svar-l&#x1e6d;loka, Indra's heaven above the sun or between it and the polar star ; Mahar-l&#x1e6d;loka, a region above the polar star and inhabited by Bh&#x1e5b;igo and other saints who survive the destruction of the 3 lower worlds ; Janar-l&#x1e6d;loka, inhabited by Brahm&#x0101;'s son Sanat-kum&#x0101;ra &amp;c. ; Tapar-l&#x1e6d;loka, inh&#x1e6d;inhabited by deified Vair&#x0101;gins ; Satya-l&#x1e6d;loka or Brahma-l&#x1e6d;loka, abode of Brahm&#x0101;, translation to which exempts from rebirth <font color="#FF0000" font size=-2><a name="p906-2"></a>[Page 906, Column 2]</font>
 ; elsewhere these 7 worlds are described as earth, sky, heaven, middle region, place of re-births, mansion of the blest, and abode of truth ; sometimes 14 worlds are mentioned, viz. the 7 above, and 7 lower regions called in the order of their descent below the earthA -tala, Vi-t&#x1e6d;tala, Su-t&#x1e6d;tala, Ras&#x0101;t&#x1e6d;tala, Tal&#x0101;t&#x1e6d;tala, Mah&#x0101;-t&#x1e6d;tala, and P&#x0101;t&#x0101;la ; <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#cf">cf.</a> RTL. 102, n. 1 <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#IW">IW.</a> 420, 1 ; 435, 1) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; N. of the number 'seven' (cf. above) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#VarB&#x1e5b;S">VarB&#x1e5b;S.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Sch">Sch.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the earth or world of human beings &amp;c. <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> &amp;c. (<em>ay&#x00e1;&#x1e43; lok&#x00e1;&#x1e25;</em>, this world' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>asa&#x00fa;</em> or <em>p&#x00e1;ro lok&#x00e1;&#x1e25;</em>, that or the other world' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; loke or <em>iha</em> <em>loke</em>, 'here on earth', opp. to <em>para-tra</em>, <em>para-loke</em> &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>k&#x1e5b;tsne</em> <em>loke</em>, 'on the whole earth') </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (also pl.) the inhabitants of the world, mankind, folk, people (sometimes opp. to 'king') <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> &amp;c </dd>

           <dd>&#x2022; ordinary life, worldly affairs, common practice or usage <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#G&#x1e5b;S">G&#x1e5b;S.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Nir">Nir.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> &amp;c. (<em>loke</em> either 'in ordinary life', 'in worldly matters' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; or, in common language, in popular speech', as opp. to <em>vede</em>, <em>chandasi</em>) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the faculty of seeing, sight (only in <em>c&#x00e1;k&#x1e63;ur-l&#x25cb;</em>, q.v.) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>lok&#x0101;n&#x0101;&#x1e43; s&#x0101;man&#x012b;</em> du. and <em>lok&#x0101;n&#x0101;&#x1e43; vrat&#x0101;ni</em> pl&#x1e46;. of S&#x0101;mans <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x0100;rshBr">&#x0100;rshBr.</a> [Cf.
